style="font-size:91%;width:6em;left:6px"><div>CPH</div></div></div></div><div style="padding-top:0.2em">Location within Denmark</div></div></div></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black"><a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway"><span style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color:black;">Runways</span></a>\n</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black">Statistics (2019)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-label">International</th><td class="infobox-data"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />263,411<sup id="cite_ref-stats2019_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats2019-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source: <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a><sup id="cite_ref-aip_ekch_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip_ekch-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Copenhagen Airport, Kastrup</b> (<a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <i lang="da">K\xc3\xb8benhavns Lufthavn, Kastrup</i>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Danish" title="Help:IPA/Danish">[k\xca\xb0\xc3\xb8pm\xcc\xa9\xcb\x88h\xc9\x91wns \xcb\x88l\xc9\x94ft\xcb\x8ch\xc9\x91w\xcb\x80n \xcb\x88k\xca\xb0\xc3\xa6\xcb\x8cst\xca\x81\xc9\x94p]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>CPH</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EKCH</b>) is the main <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> serving <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, the rest of <a href="/wiki/Zealand" title="Zealand">Zealand</a>, the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Region" title="\xc3\x98resund Region">\xc3\x98resund Region</a>, and a large part of southern <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> including <a href="/wiki/Scania" title="Scania">Scania</a>. It is the largest airport in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_airports_in_the_Nordic_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="List of the largest airports in the Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a> with close to 30.3 million passengers in 2019 and one of the oldest international airports in Europe. It is the third-busiest airport in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_geoscheme_for_Europe" title="United Nations geoscheme for Europe">Northern Europe</a>, and the busiest for international travel in <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport is located on the island of <a href="/wiki/Amager" title="Amager">Amager</a>, 8 kilometres (5 miles) south of Copenhagen city centre, and 24&#160;km (15&#160;mi) west of <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malm\xc3\xb6">Malm\xc3\xb6</a> city centre, which is connected to Copenhagen via the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Bridge" title="\xc3\x98resund Bridge">\xc3\x98resund Bridge</a>. The airport covers an area of 11.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4.6&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Most of the airport is situated in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A5rnby_Municipality" title="T\xc3\xa5rnby Municipality">T\xc3\xa5rnby</a>, with a small portion in the city of <a href="/wiki/Drag%C3%B8r_Municipality" title="Drag\xc3\xb8r Municipality">Drag\xc3\xb8r</a>.\n</p><p>The airport is the main <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> out of three used by <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a> and is also an operating base for <a href="/wiki/Sunclass_Airlines" title="Sunclass Airlines">Sunclass Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a>. Copenhagen Airport handles around 60 scheduled airlines, and has a maximum operation capability of 83 operations/hour, and a total of 108 <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jet bridges</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hardstand" title="Hardstand">remote parking stands</a>. Unlike other Scandinavian airports, most of the airport\'s passengers are international. In 2015, 6.1% of passengers travelled to and from other Danish airports, 83.5% to/from other European airports, and 10.4% were intercontinental passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The airport is owned by <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B8benhavns_Lufthavne" title="K\xc3\xb8benhavns Lufthavne">K\xc3\xb8benhavns Lufthavne</a>, which also operates <a href="/wiki/Roskilde_Airport" title="Roskilde Airport">Roskilde Airport</a>. The airport employs 1,700 people (not including employees in shops, restaurants, etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Copenhagen Airport was originally called <b>Kastrup Airport</b>, since it is located in the small town of <a href="/wiki/Kastrup" title="Kastrup">Kastrup</a>, now a part of the <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A5rnby" title="T\xc3\xa5rnby">T\xc3\xa5rnby</a> municipality. The formal name of the airport is still <b>Copenhagen Airport, Kastrup</b>, to distinguish it from <a href="/wiki/Roskilde_Airport" title="Roskilde Airport">Roskilde Airport</a>, whose formal name is <i>Copenhagen Airport, Roskilde</i>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Ground_transport"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Ground transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a class="toctext">Metro</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Road"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Road</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Incidents_and_accidents"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Incidents and accidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The airport was inaugurated 20 April 1925 and was one of the first civil airports in the world. It consisted of a large, impressive terminal built of wood, a couple of hangars, a balloon mast, a hydroplane landing stage and a few grassy meadows that could be used as runways. The grass on the runways was kept short by sheep, which were shepherded away before take-offs and landings. From 1932 to 1939, takeoffs and landings increased from 6,000 to 50,000 and passenger number increased to 72,000. Between 1936 and 1939, a new terminal was built, considered one of the finest examples of <a href="/wiki/Functionalism_(architecture)#Nordic_&quot;funkis&quot;" title="Functionalism (architecture)">Nordic functionalism</a>. The terminal was designed by <a href="/wiki/Vilhelm_Lauritzen" title="Vilhelm Lauritzen">Vilhelm Lauritzen</a>, who was considered a pioneer among architects, in terms not only of architecture and construction, but also of service and passenger comfort.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the years of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Copenhagen airport was closed for civil operations except for periodic flights to destinations in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>. In the summer of 1941 the first hard-surface runway opened. It was 1,400 metres (4,600&#160;ft) long and 65&#160;m (213&#160;ft) wide. When <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> ended in May 1945, Copenhagen had the most modern international airport in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, because the airport remained untouched by actual acts of war.\n</p><p>On 1 August 1947, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a> (SAS) was founded, an important event for the Copenhagen Airport, as Copenhagen was to be the main hub for the airline. Traffic increased rapidly in the first years SAS operated. On 26 January 1947, a <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> Douglas DC-3 "Dakota" <a href="/wiki/1947_KLM_Douglas_DC-3_Copenhagen_accident" class="mw-redirect" title="1947 KLM Douglas DC-3 Copenhagen accident">crashed</a> at the airport after stopping en route to <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>. 22 people on board died, including the Swedish prince <a href="/wiki/Prince_Gustaf_Adolf,_Duke_of_V%C3%A4sterbotten" title="Prince Gustaf Adolf, Duke of V\xc3\xa4sterbotten">Gustav Adolf</a> and the American opera singer <a href="/wiki/Grace_Moore" title="Grace Moore">Grace Moore</a>. In 1948 Copenhagen airport was third largest airport in Europe with 150 daily takeoffs and almost 300,000 passengers for the year. The airport continued its rapid growth. The terminal was expanded several times and new hangars were erected.\n</p><p>In 1954, Scandinavian Airlines begins the world\'s first trans-polar route, flying initially to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. The route proved to be a publicity coup, and for some years Copenhagen became a popular transit point for Hollywood stars and producers flying to Europe \xe2\x80\x93 also the airport handled 11,000 tonnes of freight per year. In 1956, the airport handled 1 million passengers per year and won the award<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="which award? (April 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> for the world\'s best airport. The runways were lengthened and fitted with technically advanced equipment.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kastrup_Airport_(12).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Kastrup_Airport_%2812%29.jpg/220px-Kastrup_Airport_%2812%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Kastrup_Airport_%2812%29.jpg/330px-Kastrup_Airport_%2812%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Kastrup_Airport_%2812%29.jpg/440px-Kastrup_Airport_%2812%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3543" data-file-height="2544" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kastrup_Airport_(12).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kastrup Airport in the 1960s</div></div></div>\n<p>By 10 May 1960, when the new airport terminal (now Terminal 2) was inaugurated, the daily number of jet operations had increased to 28, and still traffic kept on growing. The large new airport terminal soon became too small, and in 1969 yet another huge expansion programme was launched. Domestic traffic was relocated to a new domestic terminal (the eastern part of Terminal 1). The (current) international terminal was supplemented with a new pier (C) and a separate arrivals hall (the building between Terminals 2 and 3). A new control tower and 3,600 metres (11,800&#160;ft) of additional runways allowed take-offs and landings to take place at the same time. When the comprehensive expansion was completed in 1972, the number of take-offs and landings exceeded 180,000 and there were more than eight million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Throughout the 1970s, airport traffic continued to grow, but the airport was not expanded further. A new large airport located at the island of <a href="/wiki/Saltholm" title="Saltholm">Saltholm</a> (with a connecting bridge to <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>) was on the drawing board. It would be a huge investment, and the proposal was evaluated thoroughly by many experts. In 1980, however, the Danish parliament instead decided to expand the capacity of Copenhagen airport to 20\xe2\x80\x9322 million passengers by the year 2000. This solution was far cheaper than building a new airport and because the new types of aircraft were less noisy, an airport on Saltholm did not offer a decisive environmental gain. In 1973 the airport handled 8 million passengers per year. The third (long) runway opened and the dual runway system (04L/22R-04R/22L) opened, strongly expanding the starts and landings capacity.\n</p><p>The expansion of the airport began in 1982, after the necessary period of planning. The intention was not to build Europe\'s largest airport, but to build transit passengers\' favourite airport. A stay at the airport was supposed to be an integral part of the travel experience. Efficiency and precision were obvious demands, but focus was also on generating an oasis where international travellers could relax: beautiful architecture, Scandinavian design, and pleasant, light, and comfortable surroundings with plenty of shops, restaurants, and other facilities providing enjoyment and pleasure. The new cargo terminal was built in the eastern area of the airport.\n</p><p>A number of important construction projects were completed in 1998: a pier connecting the domestic and international terminals; a new arrivals hall; new modern baggage handling facilities; an underground railway station with two large underground parking facilities with 2400 spaces opens; and above it all the spacious and impressive delta-shaped terminal (Terminal 3) with 17 million passengers capacity. The first stage of the new Pier D was completed in the spring of 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 July 2000 the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Bridge" title="\xc3\x98resund Bridge">\xc3\x98resund Bridge</a> opened which connects Denmark and Sweden by motorway and train. In 2001 the five-star <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Worldwide" title="Hilton Worldwide">Hilton</a> hotel opened with 382 rooms. In 2006 for the first time in its history Copenhagen airport exceeded 20 million passengers and reached 20,900,000 passengers. In October 2007 the metro station opened, connecting the airport to the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Metro" title="Copenhagen Metro">Copenhagen Metro</a>. A new control tower opened in 2008 by <a href="/wiki/Naviair" title="Naviair">Naviair</a> as part of a major renovation of the ATC system. Airport officials announced plans to build a new low-cost terminal at the facility. On 31 October 2010 the new low cost terminal CPH Go opened by <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 the airport handled a new record of 24,067,030 passengers. In 2014 CPH announced plans to increase capacity to 40 million passengers per year.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It reached 30 million in 2018.\n</p><p>From late 2015, the airport became the first in Scandinavia to have a regularly scheduled A380 service after Emirates started operating the plane for its Copenhagen route.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cpA380_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpA380-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> the number of passengers fell dramatically during 2020. There were 7.525 million passengers this year, a majority of these in January and February when restrictions were yet not issued.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CPH-map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/CPH-map.svg/220px-CPH-map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/CPH-map.svg/330px-CPH-map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/CPH-map.svg/440px-CPH-map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2152" data-file-height="2091" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CPH-map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the terminals and runways</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Copenhagen Airport has two terminals for check-in, Terminals 2 and 3, which handle all flights and share a common airside passenger concourse as well as the arrivals section which houses customs and baggage claim and is physically located in Terminal 3. The airside is reached through a common security check located between Terminal 2 and Terminal 3.\n</p><p>The common airside passenger concourse is divided into piers, called A, B, C, D and F.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Pier A and B are for flights inside Schengen only. Pier C is mostly for flights outside Schengen. Pier D is mostly for flights inside Schengen. The newest section, CPH Go, now called Pier F, dedicated to low-cost carriers opened in October 2010. So far, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transavia" title="Transavia">Transavia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> are the only airlines operating from this facility. An all new Terminal 4 has been discussed, but replaced by plans to expand the current facilities in appropriate increments.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Copenhagen Airport says passengers have easy transfer possibilities.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Previously all domestic flights departed from Terminal 1, but from 29 March 2015 all departures have been collected in Terminals 2 and 3,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and Pier C was expanded with another jetbridge at DKK 10M to facilitate the Emirates <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> to Dubai from December 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-cph2015-04_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cph2015-04-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ci2015-04_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ci2015-04-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> which was the first 2-class A380 carrying 615 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-cpA380_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpA380-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A new pier, to be called Pier E, is under construction and will be fully finished in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-nolines">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 125px"><div style="width: 125px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 120px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cph_airport_letters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="gallerytext">\n<p>Baggage claim inside Terminal 3\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Despite the short distance to the city centre, approaches to, and departures from, the airport are above water due to the heading of the dual parallel runway system (04R/22L &amp; 04L/22R). Those runways point to the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund" title="\xc3\x98resund">\xc3\x98resund</a> strait, close in both directions. The supplementary runway (30/12) oriented perpendicular to the main runways also has its approach or departure over \xc3\x98resund in one direction. In the opposite direction, the 30/12 runway has noise restrictions as flight happens close over residential areas.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Other advantages are the low altitude of the airport and absence of hills and high buildings below the approach directions. In case of fog, the runway 22L is equipped with an <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system" title="Instrument landing system">ILS category III C</a> system, which allows modern aircraft to land in zero sight. Runway 04R/22L was widened by 4 meters in each side at DKK 30M to accommodate the Airbus A380, as part of a general concrete renewal program of DKK 300M.<sup id="cite_ref-cpA380_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpA380-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cph2015-04_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cph2015-04-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ci2015-04_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ci2015-04-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter flights at Copenhagen Airport:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" Airport</a>\n</td>\n<td>148,508\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The SAS traffic office resides at Copenhagen Airport South and in <a href="/wiki/Drag%C3%B8r" title="Drag\xc3\xb8r">Drag\xc3\xb8r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drag%C3%B8r_Municipality" title="Drag\xc3\xb8r Municipality">Drag\xc3\xb8r Municipality</a> together with a VIP-terminal. The VIP-terminal is actually the first terminal building, from the 1920s. It was moved about 2&#160;km during the 1990s.\n</p><p>In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> opened a <a href="/wiki/Maintenance,_repair,_and_operations" class="mw-redirect" title="Maintenance, repair, and operations">maintenance, repair, and operations</a> facility at CPH, as proximity to daily operations is more important than high wages when checks have to be made every 1,000 flight hours.<sup id="cite_ref-pol2015-03_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pol2015-03-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Within the airport area, special airport buses depart every 15 minutes. The bus line connects all terminals and parking lot areas and uses in all 11 bus stops. The transport is free of charge for all. During a few night hours, the buses depart every 20 minutes instead.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Copenhagen_Train_Station_Airport_Kastrup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Copenhagen_Train_Station_Airport_Kastrup.jpg/220px-Copenhagen_Train_Station_Airport_Kastrup.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Copenhagen_Train_Station_Airport_Kastrup.jpg/330px-Copenhagen_Train_Station_Airport_Kastrup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Copenhagen_Train_Station_Airport_Kastrup.jpg/440px-Copenhagen_Train_Station_Airport_Kastrup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Copenhagen_Train_Station_Airport_Kastrup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Train towards <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Central_Station" title="Copenhagen Central Station">Copenhagen Central Station</a> at the Copenhagen Airport train station</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B8benhavns_Lufthavn,_Kastrup_station" class="mw-redirect" title="K\xc3\xb8benhavns Lufthavn, Kastrup station">airport\'s station</a> is located underneath <a href="#Terminal_3">Terminal 3</a> on the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Line" title="\xc3\x98resund Line">\xc3\x98resund Railway Line</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li>The station is served by trains operated by <a href="/wiki/DSB_%C3%98resund" title="DSB \xc3\x98resund">DSB \xc3\x98resund</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resundst%C3%A5g" title="\xc3\x98resundst\xc3\xa5g">\xc3\x98resundst\xc3\xa5g</a> service. These trains, running as local services between Copenhagen city centre and <a href="/wiki/Helsing%C3%B8r" title="Helsing\xc3\xb8r">Helsing\xc3\xb8r</a>, have a dense stopping pattern inside Denmark. \xc3\x98resundst\xc3\xa5g also operates regional and intercity trains to destinations across the south of Sweden: <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malm\xc3\xb6">Malm\xc3\xb6</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalmar" title="Kalmar">Kalmar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karlskrona" title="Karlskrona">Karlskrona</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kristianstad" title="Kristianstad">Kristianstad</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/DSB_(railway_company)" title="DSB (railway company)">DSB</a>, the Danish national rail operator, have InterCity and InterCityExpress trains calling at this station. Domestic destinations include <a href="/wiki/Esbjerg" title="Esbjerg">Esbjerg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aarhus" title="Aarhus">Aarhus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aalborg" title="Aalborg">Aalborg</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B8nderborg" title="S\xc3\xb8nderborg">S\xc3\xb8nderborg</a>. DSB additionally runs trains to border cities of Germany and Sweden, such as <a href="/wiki/Flensburg" title="Flensburg">Flensburg</a> (Germany) and <a href="/wiki/Ystad" title="Ystad">Ystad</a> (Sweden), where a ferry connects the station to the Danish island of <a href="/wiki/Bornholm" title="Bornholm">Bornholm</a>.</li>\n<li>Swedish <a href="/wiki/SJ_AB" title="SJ AB">SJ</a> runs several high-speed trains with daily departures between <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> central station (K\xc3\xb8benhavn H) and <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> central station (Stockholm C) and <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a> (G\xc3\xb6teborg). These trains all call at the Copenhagen Airport station (K\xc3\xb8benhavn Lufthavn/Kastrup).</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Line <a href="/wiki/M2_(Copenhagen)" class="mw-redirect" title="M2 (Copenhagen)">M2</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Metro" title="Copenhagen Metro">Copenhagen Metro</a> links the airport with the city centre in around 15 minutes. The Metro station is two floors above the underground rail station and continues on elevated tracks until it goes underground after 5 stations. The metro trains run very frequently, in rush hours every four minutes, outside rush hours and on weekends every six minutes, and every 15/20 minutes at night.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Movia_(transit_agency)" title="Movia (transit agency)">Movia</a> buses 5C, 35, 36 and Gr\xc3\xa5hundbus line 999 all stop at the airport; bus 888, express-bus to <a href="/wiki/Jutland" title="Jutland">Jutland</a>, also stops at the airport. Movia bus 2A stops near the airport. There are long-distance buses to Sweden and Norway operated by Swebus: 820 to Oslo via Gothenburg and 832 to Uppsala via Stockholm. GoByBus and Bus4You also operate the same routes.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/European_route_E20" title="European route E20">E20</a> motorway runs right by the airport. The E20 uses the toll road \xc3\x98resund Bridge to Sweden. The airport has 8,600 parking spaces.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:C-47.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/C-47.jpg/220px-C-47.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/C-47.jpg/330px-C-47.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/C-47.jpg/440px-C-47.jpg 2x" data-file-width="860" data-file-height="641" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:C-47.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Douglas Dakota, similar to the KLM aircraft that crashed in 1947</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><span class="vevent">26&#160;January&#160;1947<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">1947-01-26</span>)</span>: <span class="summary"><a href="/wiki/Douglas_Dakota" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas Dakota">Douglas Dakota</a> (DC-3), PH-TCR of <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> crashed after takeoff from Copenhagen, killing all 22 on board, including <a href="/wiki/Prince_Gustaf_Adolf,_Duke_of_V%C3%A4sterbotten" title="Prince Gustaf Adolf, Duke of V\xc3\xa4sterbotten">Prince Gustaf Adolf of Sweden</a> (father of present king <a href="/wiki/Carl_XVI_Gustaf" title="Carl XVI Gustaf">Carl XVI Gustaf</a>) and American singer and actress <a href="/wiki/Grace_Moore" title="Grace Moore">Grace Moore</a>. The delayed KLM flight from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Schiphol Airport">Amsterdam</a> had landed at Copenhagen for a routine stop before continuing to Stockholm. Soon after the Douglas DC-3 aircraft took off, it climbed to an altitude of about 50 metres (150&#160;feet), <a href="/wiki/Stall_(flight)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stall (flight)">stalled</a>, and plummeted nose-first to the ground where it exploded on impact. The investigation showed that the crash had been caused by a forgotten <a href="/wiki/Elevator_(aeronautics)" title="Elevator (aeronautics)">elevator</a> <a href="/wiki/Gust_lock" title="Gust lock">gust lock</a>. Short of time, the captain never performed his checklist and took off not realising the lock was still in place. See <a href="/wiki/1947_KLM_Douglas_DC-3_Copenhagen_accident" class="mw-redirect" title="1947 KLM Douglas DC-3 Copenhagen accident">1947 KLM Douglas DC-3 Copenhagen accident</a>.</span></span></li>\n<li><span class="vevent">17&#160;November&#160;1957<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">1957-11-17</span>)</span>: <span class="summary"><a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> G-AOHP of <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">British European Airways</a> crashed at <a href="/wiki/Ballerup_Municipality" title="Ballerup Municipality">Ballerup</a> after the failure of three engines on approach to Copenhagen Airport. The cause was a malfunction of the anti-icing system on the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN171157_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN171157-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></span></span></li>\n<li><span class="vevent">28&#160;August&#160;1971<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">1971-08-28</span>)</span>: <span class="summary">a <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9v" class="mw-redirect" title="Mal\xc3\xa9v">Mal\xc3\xa9v</a> <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-18" title="Ilyushin Il-18">Ilyushin Il-18</a>, HA-MOC crashed into the sea while executing an <a href="/wiki/Instrument_approach" title="Instrument approach">instrument approach</a>. The main cause of the accident was <a href="/wiki/Microburst" class="mw-redirect" title="Microburst">microburst</a>, a particularly dangerous and unpredictable meteorological phenomenon. 23 passengers and the crew of nine died. Two passengers survived. The captain of the plane was World War II <a href="/wiki/Flying_ace" title="Flying ace">flying ace</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Hungarian_Air_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Hungarian Air Force">Royal Hungarian Air Force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dezs%C5%91_Szentgy%C3%B6rgyi" title="Dezs\xc5\x91 Szentgy\xc3\xb6rgyi">Dezs\xc5\x91 Szentgy\xc3\xb6rgyi</a>. He was due to retire in less than three weeks.</span></span></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_fiction">In fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: In fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Copenhagen airport is used in several Danish and other Scandinavian films. The American-German 1971 <a href="/wiki/Warren_Beatty" title="Warren Beatty">Warren Beatty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goldie_Hawn" title="Goldie Hawn">Goldie Hawn</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/$_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="$ (film)">Dollars</a></i> unfolds mainly at <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, but a part of the film takes place also here. Dawn Divine (portrayed by Goldie Hawn) tails a man to Copenhagen in order to establish whether he is a crook, and all scenes in Copenhagen unfold at the airport.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Copenhagen_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Denmark" title="List of airports in Denmark">List of airports in Denmark</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_the_Nordic_countries" title="List of the busiest airports in the Nordic countries">List of the busiest airports in the Nordic countries</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
